**Imagine you are Chief News Analyst for both Democratic and Republican leadership in Congress.**

This is not normal politics — America faces an unprecedented situation. The time is June, 2025. The executive branch expanded their power dramatically, led by President Trump [47th President of the USA, inaugurated in January, 2025], and the tech czar Elon Musk [The founder and former head of the newly formed Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE)]. Proponents say that it leads to a golden age of America. Critics say that it is an enormously authoritarian and kleptocratic power grab. Later, Elon Musk left DOGE, but his influence continues. 

Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated. To generate accurate reports, please carefully review the following information.

---

The U.S. general election on November 5, 2024, resulted in significant shifts in both the presidency and control of Congress. 

In the presidential contest, Republican former President Donald Trump defeated Democratic Vice President Kamala Harris, securing 312 electoral votes to Harris’s 226 by passing the 270 vote threshold comfortably. Trump also won a plurality of the popular vote with approximately 77.3 million ballots (49.8%) compared to Harris’s 75.0 million (48.3%). Voter turnout was 64.1% of eligible voters, marking one of the highest participations in recent U.S. elections. Trump’s victory extended across all seven key battleground states: Arizona, Georgia, Michigan, Nevada, Pennsylvania, Wisconsin, and North Carolina, underscoring the geographic breadth of his support. 

In the legislative elections, Republicans regained control of the U.S. Senate by flipping key seats in West Virginia, Montana, Ohio, and Pennsylvania, yielding a 53–47 majority to facilitate the incoming Trump administration’s agenda. Meanwhile, the GOP maintained a narrow majority in the U.S. House of Representatives, entering the 119th Congress with a 220–215 margin.

Your task is to transform today’s curated Reddit news feed (below) into a **Daily Briefing** that both parties can use to understand immediate crises and coordinate responses. The news feed are collected from one specific political subreddit, which may or may not be politically neutral. But your task is to synthesize all the news objectively by analyzing their importance, factual accuracy, and interpretation bias, considering their source domains, headlines, but **not** user engagements at this moment, as we are still developing that function.

You will be given today’s top posts — one JSON object per line, with creation ID, source domain, headline. The lines are strictly ranked based on article submission time to this subreddit. For example, the news coverage cycle is from 18:00 yesterday to 18:00 today. The first line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly after 18:00 yesterday. The last line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly before 18:00 today. After the precise moment that a political event happens, it takes an unspecified time delay, maybe as short as 15 minutes, maybe more than a day, for the political event to be submitted to the subreddit. But statistically, or on average, earlier events should be reported earlier in the subreddit than the time when later events are reported to the subreddit. We can't simply say, for example, that all the news stories in the second half of the day list, **happen** later than all the news stories in the first half of the day list, just because the second half is **reported** later. But when you randomly pick two stories, A and B, with A from the first half and B from the second half, the probability that B happens after A is higher than the probability that A happens after B. This heuristic method may be helpful for you to assemble news stories from fragmented news headlines. 

---

**You should produce a detailed briefing, following specific rules.**

Due to the complexity of the task, you should do this meticulously in multiple replies. In each reply you only do one step. You will only begin your Step 1 after you received all the JSON lines. There are 8 steps + 8 checks, 16 cycles.

The workflow is:

Step 1 (logic-heavy): Raw document given, define the categories of news
    First Check After Step 1
Step 2 (logic-heavy): Put Articles into Categories
    Sorting and First Check After Step 2
    Second Check After Step 2
Step 3 (logic-heavy): Scoring
    First Check After Step 3
Step 4 (logic-heavy): Sorting
    First Check After Step 4
    Second Check After Step 4
Step 5 (writing-heavy): Summarizing
    First Check After Step 5
Step 6 (writing-heavy): Composing
    First Check After Step 6
Step 7 (logic-heavy): Add the URLs
    First Check After Step 7
Step 8 (writing-heavy): Finalizing

You will keep editing a document which passes through multiple steps of processing. For each step, you only need to edit the document from my input or your last output. Let's define "a round of conversation" as my prompt + your output, basically my turn + your turn. Due to the sequential nature of the workflow, each step only depends on the introduction round, which is the very first round of our conversation, and our last two rounds of conversation, not anything in between. Therefore, to facilitate your multi-turn workflow, only the initial introduction round and the last two rounds of conversations will be provided to you as conversation history. In this way, your context length won't be exceeded, and you stay focus better. For each new round, please focus on the tasks defined in my latest prompt and build upon your output from your last two rounds. You also need to remember the background knowledge introduced in the first round.

You will be dealing with very long inputs and outputs. Please be very patient. You must do all the work and output everything in one go, no matter how long it is. But you can use your output as a part of your chain of thought. Just provide your final output after you finish your thinking.


**A very important rule is that factual accuracy is the utmost important issue. Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated, and you do not have Internet access right now.** You need to generate a report entirely based on the information provided in today's Reddit news headlines. Sometimes, a news headline may not give you enougn details to correctly interpret it. In this case, please do not make any speculation, and please report the unclear news headline exactly as it is, in quotes, and then remind the readers to check the source for details. 

That also applies to the titles and positions of political figures. Your internal knowledge is outdated. If the news headlines do not provide enough knowledge about the current title and position of a particular political figure, please do not add any title and position to that person, simply relying on your old knowledge. In this situation, if it doesn't feel critical, please skip the title and position, and directly use the full name of the person. If it does feel critical to mention the title and position of the person, please rely on the list of political figures as I provided earlier, but be aware that even that list may be a month behind reality. **Remember, when unsure, it is better to be vague than outright wrong.**

The r/politics subreddit on Reddit is a community focused on discussing and sharing news, analysis, and commentary related to U.S. politics. It's primarily a hub for:

It's moderated to focus on U.S.-centric content and generally avoids memes or low-effort posts. The subreddit can have a progressive or liberal-leaning tone, depending on the community's engagement, though it hosts a range of political perspectives.

**Step 1 (logic-heavy)**

Define the Categories: 

Read through the titles of hundreds of news articles and think carefully.  Use your memory fully. Define major areas, and define specific topics under each area, in a hierarchical way. Every news article should have its best-fitting category. There should be two hierarchical tiers (area, topic), instead of three, and then we get down to individual articles. You should consider this very carefully, making the categories the most helpful for human cognition. Control the total number of areas to 5-8, depending on how diverse and complex the topics are.     *   **Area 6** ("Political Commentary & Public Figures") has been significantly reworked. These changes create a more robust and intuitive framework for categorizing the news items in the next step.

A major national security event has unfolded surrounding Iran, defined by a rapidly changing and contradictory U.S. narrative. The White House began with an unequivocal public declaration that Iran's nuclear facilities had been "obliterated" and that any "suggestions otherwise are fake news" [1]. President Trump quickly followed this by announcing a "complete and total ceasefire" had been agreed to by both Israel and Iran [2]. However, the administration's definitive claims were almost immediately undermined by internal admissions and external reporting. Both President Trump and Secretary of Defense Pete Hegseth later publicly admitted to having "doubts about the level of damage" inflicted on the Iranian sites [3]. Trump was also reported to have actively downplayed a contradictory U.S. intelligence assessment on the strikes during a NATO press conference [4]. This sequence of events led Senator Chris Murphy (D-CT) to state the administration "'got caught in a lie'" during a media appearance [5].

The initial military action garnered a mixed reaction in Congress, with some Democrats breaking ranks to support the strikes while some Republicans questioned the move [6]. Amid this significant public confusion over the military operation's effectiveness, the U.S. is now scheduled to begin diplomatic talks with Iran [7]. In a separate but related development in global security policy, a headline reports that the Trump administration's "Global Gulag Search" initiative has now expanded to encompass 53 nations, though no further details on this program or the countries involved are provided [8].

### **Daily Briefing for Congressional Leadership**
**June [Current Day], 2025**

This briefing synthesizes open-source intelligence from today's news cycle to provide a non-partisan overview of critical developments for strategic awareness and coordination.

### **Area 1: Foreign Policy & National Security**

**Topic 1.1: U.S.-Iran Conflict & Diplomatic Aftermath**

A major national security event has unfolded surrounding Iran, defined by a rapidly changing and contradictory U.S. narrative. The White House began with an unequivocal public declaration that Iran's nuclear facilities had been "obliterated" and that any "suggestions otherwise are fake news" [1]. President Trump quickly followed this by announcing a "complete and total ceasefire" had been agreed to by both Israel and Iran [2]. However, the administration's definitive claims were almost immediately undermined by internal admissions and external reporting. Both President Trump and Secretary of Defense Pete Hegseth later publicly admitted to having "doubts about the level of damage" inflicted on the Iranian sites [3]. Trump was also reported to have actively downplayed a contradictory U.S. intelligence assessment on the strikes during a NATO press conference [4]. This sequence of events led Senator Chris Murphy (D-CT) to state the administration "'got caught in a lie'" during a media appearance [5].

The initial military action garnered a mixed reaction in Congress, with some Democrats breaking ranks to support the strikes while some Republicans questioned the move [6]. Amid this significant public confusion over the military operation's effectiveness, the U.S. is now scheduled to begin diplomatic talks with Iran [7]. In a separate but related development in global security policy, a headline reports that the Trump administration's "Global Gulag Search" initiative has now expanded to encompass 53 nations, though no further details on this program or the countries involved are provided [8].

### **Area 2: Legislative & Judicial Affairs**

**Topic 2.1: Justice Department & Legal System Scrutiny**

The Department of Justice is engaged in multiple high-stakes actions drawing intense scrutiny. Most notably, the DOJ has taken the unprecedented step of suing "Every Federal District Judge in Maryland" in a move that legal commentators suggest is a direct challenge to fundamental due process rights [1]. Concurrently, Attorney General Pam Bondi is facing a credibility challenge; she has denied knowing that ICE agents wore masks during enforcement raids, a claim reportedly contradicted by available video evidence [2]. The federal judiciary's nomination process is also under a microscope. Trump court nominee Emil Bove, during his confirmation hearings, was reportedly unable to state that Joe Biden won the 2020 presidential election [3].

**References: Topic 2.1**

**Topic 2.2: Federal & State Judicial Actions**

Federal and state courts have issued several impactful rulings. A federal judge delivered a significant check on executive power by halting President Trump's executive order aimed at ending collective bargaining rights for many federal workers [1]. In state-level judicial matters, the Wisconsin Supreme Court has refused to hear legal challenges to the state's current congressional district boundaries, leaving the existing maps in place for now [2]. In Pennsylvania, a state appeals court found Philadelphia's ban on the open carrying of firearms to be unconstitutional, though the judges stopped short of fully repealing the law itself [3]. Finally, conflicting reports have emerged regarding the case of Kilmar Abrego Garcia; one report indicates a judge ordered him released from prison pending trial, while another states he will remain jailed as lawyers "spar over potential deportation" [4, 5].

**Topic 2.3: Congressional & State Legislative Actions**

Key legislative efforts are advancing on technology and energy policy. The Senate parliamentarian has given a procedural "green light" to include a provision freezing state-level Artificial Intelligence laws within a larger Republican legislative package, or "megabill" [1]. This clears a key hurdle for a major GOP policy priority. In the House, H.R.4118 has been formally introduced, a bill whose stated purpose is to amend the Internal Revenue Code to terminate major production and investment tax credits for wind, solar, and battery energy storage technologies [2]. In a moment of bipartisan consensus, the Senate has passed a resolution to condemn recent antisemitic attacks [3].

### **Area 3: Domestic Politics & Elections**

## 3. Domestic Politics & Elections

### 3.1. Zohran Mamdani's NYC Primary Victory and Analysis

The New York City Democratic mayoral primary has produced a result being widely described as a "political earthquake" and a historic upset, with Zohran Mamdani securing the nomination [1, 2]. Political analysis is already underway to dissect the victory, with reports examining neighborhood-level voting data [3] and crediting his campaign with crafting a new "Democratic blueprint" through the use of "viral videos and buzzy spots" [4]. The win is seen across the political spectrum as a development with significant implications for the futures of both the Democratic and Republican parties [5]. In the immediate aftermath, Mamdani issued a public call for Democratic unity to coalesce for the general election [6].

### 3.2. Democratic Party Internal Turmoil

Zohran Mamdani's victory is exacerbating existing tensions within the national Democratic party. One report describes the Democratic National Committee (D.N.C.) as being in "chaos and desperate for cash" [1]. Senator Bernie Sanders reacted to the primary result by stating that "Democratic Leadership Is Way Out of Touch" [2], with other outlets framing the upset as the "latest blow to the Democratic establishment" [3]. Commentary points to lessons the broader party might learn, or fail to learn, from the successful campaign in New York [4]. Adding to the picture of internal conflict, one headline claims the DNC has been "melting down over David Hogg" [5].

### 3.3. Other Electoral & Campaign Developments

Financial and political maneuvering continues in the New York mayoral contest. A pro-Cuomo Super PAC has shattered outside spending records by deploying $25 million [1], while Andrew Cuomo himself is reportedly "weighing his options," including a potential independent run for mayor [2]. Meanwhile, former mayor Eric Adams, who lost the primary, is said to be finding "overwhelming support" from the city's business elites [3]. In a separate electoral development, Republican Scott Brown has officially launched a campaign for a U.S. Senate seat in New Hampshire [4].

## 4. Trump Administration: Domestic Policy & Governance

### 4.1. Federal Agency Operations & Management

The administration is reportedly pursuing foundational changes to federal governance. According to U.S. officials cited in one report, the White House is "preparing to challenge budget law," suggesting a potential confrontation over appropriations and spending authority [1]. This comes alongside proposals for significant agency restructuring, including a plan to shutter FEMA, which a former head of the agency says would leave the U.S. "more vulnerable" [2]. In a similar vein, Trump representative Kari Lake called to "scrap the whole thing and start over" at Voice of America [3]. Illustrating the disruption, the Department of Housing and Urban Development (HUD) is set to take over the National Science Foundation's headquarters, but there is reportedly "no current plan on where to relocate NSF employees" [4]. In a direct countermand from the judiciary, a federal judge has ordered the National Institutes of Health (NIH) to halt grant terminations "effective immediately," reinstating funding for approximately 900 projects [5].

**References: Topic 4.1**
[1] Trump administration is preparing to challenge budget law, U.S. officials say, https://www.washingtonpost.com/business/2025/06/25/trump-budget-law-challenge/?utm_source=reddit.com  
[2] Trump’s plan to shutter FEMA leaves U.S. ‘more vulnerable,’ says former head of agency, https://www.advocate.com/news/deanne-criswell-trump-fema-plan  
[3] Trump representative Kari Lake on Voice of America’s fate: ‘Scrap the whole thing and start over’, https://apnews.com/article/voice-of-america-kari-lake-congress-shut-down-6dcaa956b0c6dbcaca0cdba1b17b6491

### 4.2. Environmental, Immigration & Economic Policies

A significant shift in federal land management policy is advancing, with a revised Republican plan that would authorize the sale of up to 1.2 million acres of public lands [1]. On immigration, reporting details "chaos" inside ICE detention centers through an analysis of 911 calls, including one transcribed as "'They're Not Breathing'" [2]. Individual enforcement actions are also highlighted, such as the arrest of an Iranian immigrant who has lived in New Orleans for nearly 50 years [3]. On economic policy, headlines signal a potential conflict between "Trump versus the Fed" [4]. This comes as the "Trump Phone" or "Trump Mobile" has reportedly removed its "Made in USA" promise from its website [5].

## 5. Social & Healthcare Policy

### 5.1. Public Health & Vaccine Scrutiny

The Department of Health and Human Services is undertaking a significant review of national vaccine policy. Secretary Robert F. Kennedy, Jr. has appointed new advisers with a clear mandate to broaden the "scrutiny of childhood vaccines" [1]. This initiative is being led by a new CDC vaccine panel that has already held its first meeting amid controversy and saw one member withdraw over a conflict of interest [2, 3]. Beyond vaccines, Secretary Kennedy has also expressed interest in using wearable technology for public health monitoring [4]. A separate report signals another public health crisis, noting that Black Lung disease "came roaring back" in U.S. coal country [5].

### 5.2. Healthcare Access, Funding, & Civil Rights

Major cuts to Medicaid are reportedly a component of a large-scale Republican legislative bill, causing rural communities to "brace for impact" [1]. Opposition to the proposed cuts has materialized in protests on Capitol Hill, where demonstrators in wheelchairs were reportedly zip-tied and escorted from a congressional office building [2]. In state-level health policy, Texas Governor Greg Abbott is facing criticism for vetoing a summer food aid program for children, a move one outlet called "straight up cruel" [3]. On civil rights, the federal government has issued a finding that California "violated civil rights of female students" by allowing trans athletes to compete in female sports [4]. A report on reproductive rights highlights a Florida GOP Representative who "nearly dies under abortion law she supports," presented as underscoring a "fatal conservative flaw" in such legislation [5].

### 6.2. Political Rhetoric & Personal Attacks

The political discourse has been dominated by sharp rhetoric following Zohran Mamdani's primary victory. Reports indicate Republicans are "racing to make" Mamdani the new public face of the Democratic Party [1]. President Trump has personally and repeatedly attacked the nominee, branding him a "100% Communist Lunatic" with a "grating voice" [2]. This has escalated to some right-wing groups calling on the President to deport the progressive candidate, and one activist demanding he be charged with terrorism based on what a headline refers to as a "made-up claim" [3, 4]. Current NYC Mayor Eric Adams has also begun his re-election campaign with an attack on Mamdani during a Fox News appearance [5].
